  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1b96ebfe-ef2d-4cd0-9447-a4431401cdaa'
      });

<div id="bookReviews">
  




  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_152114719" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152114719" />
    <a title="merg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1859472-merg"><img alt="merg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548127244p2/1859472.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152114719?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="merg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="merg" href="/user/show/1859472-merg">merg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152114719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8468137376927150349">They have the cover picture up for this already?! Wow. Hey, I think that's Lionblaze on the cover! He finally gets a cover picture after what, 10 books with him as one of the main characters? <br/><br/>(That was my short little review I wrote before the book came out that got more comments than any review I've written before. Now, on to the REAL review.)<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Wow. The Forgotten Warrior was really good! Much better than Sign of the Moon. After that one, I was a bit worried that the condition of th</span></span>
  <span id="freeText8468137376927150349" style="display:none">They have the cover picture up for this already?! Wow. Hey, I think that's Lionblaze on the cover! He finally gets a cover picture after what, 10 books with him as one of the main characters? <br /><br />(That was my short little review I wrote before the book came out that got more comments than any review I've written before. Now, on to the REAL review.)<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Wow. The Forgotten Warrior was really good! Much better than Sign of the Moon. After that one, I was a bit worried that the condition of the Warriors series was starting to deteriorate a bit. The Forgotten Warrior restored my faith. :) The characters were in character, and I thought that Dovewing and Ivypool's personalities were deepened nicely. Poor Ivypool. Some of those Dark Forest scenes were creepily intense. I felt so bad for Ivypool when she had to "kill" Antpelt. I really liked the last line in that chapter:<br /><br /><i> Every sacrifice I make is for the good of my Clan--and for the other Clans around the lake. Even if that means sacrificing myself. </i><br /><br />It was chillingly sad. I liked Ivypool a lot better than in the other books. <br /><br />The title of the book seems to refer to two different cats. Both Hollyleaf and Sol returned to ThunderClan. I was expecting Hollyleaf--Sol, not so much. Let me just say, Sol really irritates me. Hollyleaf used to irritate me a bit, but her personality seems to have changed during her time in the tunnels. To me, she's much more likable now.<br /><br />I hope that Lionblaze and Cinderheart can resolve their issues. Cinderheart is one of my favorite characters, but I like her better as Cinderheart than Cinderpelt. I wish she would stop being so thickheaded and live her life the way she wants, rather than the way she feels bound by duty to follow. I think that in this case, it's better for her. <br /><br />And, of course, there was Jayfeather. :) He's still my favorite. The thing I don't like about Omen of the Stars is the fact that there are more viewpoints, so Jayfeather's isn't chosen as frequently. I was happy when he stood up for himself after being accused of murder. Really, though--do those cats seriously think a blind medicine cat, no matter how awesome of a blind medicine cat, could manage murder? Why did Dawnpelt get so nasty? I kind of liked her when she and her brothers were first introduced, but now the only one I really like is Flametail, and, uh, he died. <br /><br />I still think that some of the Erin Hunters have seen The Lion King. All the talk about their ancestors living in the stars makes me think of Mufasa's conversation with Simba. Also, when Hollyleaf had Sol at her mercy and basically told him to run away and never return, I was thinking, "Lion King again..." Maybe it's all some weird coincidence, but I like to think it isn't. I make subtle references to The Lion King when I get stuck in the stories I write. Maybe real authors do it, too. :) <br /><br />I'm really anxious for The Last Hope! I've heard that Firestar's going to die. If that really happens, I'm going to be rather distraught. I mean, it's <i>Firestar!</i> Even if he's not my favorite character, I still like him. I'm also worried about who the next leader will be. Somehow I can't see Brambeclaw becoming Bramblestar. That would mean he'd have to either die or be replaced by a new deputy, though, and I really don't want that. Brambleclaw is one of my favorites! My guess is that the leader will be either Lionblaze, Graystripe, or Hollyleaf. I could be totally wrong. I'm not looking forward for the series to end. It's going to be hard to say goodbye to all the wonderful characters. I'll miss them. Hopefully the fifth series will be really good. <br /><br />So. There's my long, rambling review of The Forgotten Warrior. All my reviews of the Warriors books are kind of weird. I think it's because I'm usually in a state of hyper euphoria/anxiety when I finish each new Warriors book...<br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8468137376927150349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_172673178" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172673178" />
    <a title="Whitlea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5538129-whitlea"><img alt="Whitlea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309658467p2/5538129.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172673178?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitlea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitlea" href="/user/show/5538129-whitlea">Whitlea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5538129-whitlea?shelf=warriors">warriors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172673178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9568610674041674449">This was definitely the best book out of Omen of the Stars, and better than any book of Power of Three. <br/><br/>This book is why I have stuck with Warriors for over three years. It had all the excitment a book from this series should, enough surprises and plot twists to keep things interesting, and it answered enough questions, while leaving enough for the fans to ponder over too. <br/><br/>I can honestly say that after getting past the first few chapters, I was not bored once while reading this book, something t</span>
  <span id="freeText9568610674041674449" style="display:none">This was definitely the best book out of Omen of the Stars, and better than any book of Power of Three. <br /><br />This book is why I have stuck with Warriors for over three years. It had all the excitment a book from this series should, enough surprises and plot twists to keep things interesting, and it answered enough questions, while leaving enough for the fans to ponder over too. <br /><br />I can honestly say that after getting past the first few chapters, I was not bored once while reading this book, something that isn't true of the other books from Omen of the Stars. I thought that this was going to be the most predictable Warriors book yet after reading the beginning, but I was quickly proven wrong. <br /><br />Without giving to much away, I think that this book does a great job of building up towards the ending, and that it is a great finish for the fifth book of the series.<br /><br />All in all, I would say that this book is well worth any Warriors fan's time. There are several old characters returning (not all of them in the way you would expect) and plenty of the action and drama that makes reading Warriors so much fun. 4.5/5<br /><br />And for a more indepth look at the content of the book...<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Hollyleaf returns... which I think almost everyone saw coming at this point. I think her return was handled well. It's obvious that her time away has allowed her to mature, while she still stays true to her character. She still follows the code to the very end.<br /><br />Sol's return surprised me. I will admit I did not see that coming at all. I'm tempted to pick up the SkyClan manga now to see how he was burned so badly by the Clans. I'm hoping he will return in the next book, but I'll be okay if he does not. I'm guessing there's going to be a ton of stuff happening already. I am just glad that some of his loose ends are finally wrapped up, such as why he has such an interest in the Clans.<br /><br />Briarlight is going to be Jayfeather's apprentice. Calling it now. <br /><br />Cinderheart, where to begin... I'm so glad that she's finally found out about her past life as Cinderpelt! I've been waiting for this ever since The New Prophecy. xD She's going through identity confusion, but I think at the end she finally figured out that she can be a Warrior. The only thing I would be disappointed about is that Cinderpelt as a character might be virtually gone from the series, if Cinderheart continues with her new life. Though I doubt she'll forget her life as Cinderpelt...<br /><br />Lionblaze admitting Squirrelflight was a good mother was sweet. Perhaps he'll finally be able to forgive her and Leafpool (and Hollyleaf and Jayfeather will as well)... <br /><br />It's impressive how much Ivypool has grown as a character. She's come so far from being that jealous apprentice. Now she's willing to sacrifice everything for her Clan. Granted, it was awful that she killed Antpelt. Hopefully there is a nice afterlife after the one the cats know. <br /><br />StarClan really aren't that wise anymore. I guess it's an interesting take on the afterlife. Though I wouldn't want to go there. xD<br /><br />Dawnpelt's aggression was surprising, but understandable, though not excusable. I wonder how this all will turn out for Jayfeather. Not well, I imagine. Though I'm glad that he was able to stand his ground and stand up for himself. He would never kill Flametail. <br /><br />WindClan's agression is getting pretty bad. It won't bode well for the future. I hope Onestar chews those warriors out for such a stupid attack. Exciting battle though, with a nice build up. It made an excellent conclusion to the novel.<br /><br />I can't wait to see how all this plays out in The Last Hope!<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9568610674041674449" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Kayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/712048-kayla"><img alt="Kayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567374751p2/712048.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86755866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer558753587342736292">The final battle is growing ever so closer. Lionblaze, Jayfeather, and Dovewing struggle to find the forth cat in the prophecy to save the clans. But in the midst of their struggles Sol returns. He (of course) is back to his old bag of tricks. But is he truly the forgotten warrior? After all he was never a warrior to begin with... No, the forgotten warrior is a different cat. (Take your best guess :) )<br/><br/>I loved the plot of this book. It was much better than the last warrior book. Dark Forest is br</span>
  <span id="freeText558753587342736292" style="display:none">The final battle is growing ever so closer. Lionblaze, Jayfeather, and Dovewing struggle to find the forth cat in the prophecy to save the clans. But in the midst of their struggles Sol returns. He (of course) is back to his old bag of tricks. But is he truly the forgotten warrior? After all he was never a warrior to begin with... No, the forgotten warrior is a different cat. (Take your best guess :) )<br /><br />I loved the plot of this book. It was much better than the last warrior book. Dark Forest is brainwashing even more clan cats to join and train amongst their ranks. Ivypool works undercover to discover the time and place of the final battle. She learns that the time is drawing ever closer. But when the time comes will she be able to get out alive or will Dark Forest cats take her down before she can alert Firestar? Loved this book! :) I finished it the day I got it. I wish I could build a time machine, travel forward in time and get The Last Hope. Read it. And get an autographed copy of The Last Hope. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="558753587342736292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_159697706" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159697706" />
    <a title="Micheline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4845030-micheline"><img alt="Micheline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520260852p2/4845030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159697706?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Micheline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Micheline" href="/user/show/4845030-micheline">Micheline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=creature-characters">creature-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159697706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9268501710542341797">The Forgotten Warrior, the long awaited book 5 in the Omen of the Stars (OotS) series of the Warriors book. And the second to last book of the series as we know it. According to the authors, the next series of Warrior Cats isn't written; and would take place at the beginning of the clans, kind of like prequels. I was worried I'd be confused; having finished the previous OotS Warriors book in June; but there are always short and sweet little reminders thrown in, which aren't excessive; cause I di</span>
  <span id="freeText9268501710542341797" style="display:none">The Forgotten Warrior, the long awaited book 5 in the Omen of the Stars (OotS) series of the Warriors book. And the second to last book of the series as we know it. According to the authors, the next series of Warrior Cats isn't written; and would take place at the beginning of the clans, kind of like prequels. I was worried I'd be confused; having finished the previous OotS Warriors book in June; but there are always short and sweet little reminders thrown in, which aren't excessive; cause I didn't notice them previously when I was reading each book back to back...but just enough in this case to refresh my memory. This book picks up about a month after the events of 'Sign of the Moon' book 4 in the 6 book OotS series. The battle of the Dark Forest looms ever closer, the Dark Forest cats are still recruiting heavily, training cats from all four clans in their dreams. As always I find the dream-walker element of the Warriors series fascinating. All these cats being trained separately and almost like a second clan is causing rifts within the traditional clan structures...then when a stranger appears within ThunderClan <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ a returning stranger; one that I can't wait till he gets what's coming to him lol  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> spreading more mistrust and fear...well let`s just say there's never a dull moment within the clans.<br /><br />As always, the writing style is delightful; light and easy to fall into again even considering I had read the previous book almost 6 months ago. The pacing is quick, the action is violent and brutal, and the plot thickens with secrets and prophecies. Everything we`ve grown addicted to when we started reading the Warriors series, way back when. I had forgotten how much fun it is to read from a cat's perspective (lol) Its surprisingly human; but with some unique differences: The narrative is more instinctual, a lot of information comes from the senses; what they hear, what they smell, what they see and what they taste and feel. It's fascinating to read from a perspective other than human, a refreshing change from the day to day fiction. Also the clan dynamic is still as much fun for me. The hierarchy of it all, the code the warriors live by, and how certain warriors bend it more often then others...I really had missed it all!<br /><br />Jayfeather is as usual, my favorite perspective to read: he's moody and defensive, but I love his special powers. His ehnhanced empathy (knowing what other cats are feeling), his hightened intuition and his dreams of course. I especially love when he visits other warriors dreams. He can even transform their dreaming environment to suit his purpose. Even to places he's never been in times before he was born. I'm happy that he uses it for good and I'm still further fascinated with his powers... He's still so intruiguing to me; a blind cat who almost sees better than the rest of the clan. Out of all the warrior series, he's definitely one of my all time favorites...with Brambleclaw and Firestar of course. I really enjoy Lionblaze's perspective as well, not only for his special powers and part in the prophecy, but for his venture into the dark forest and how it built his character...very like Brambleclaw who he thought was his father what seems like so long ago. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Hollyleaf! in the most anti-climatic surprise of the series (seriously, who didn't know she was in the tunnels at this point) but I was hoping for a better reveal than that. <br />Despite the anticlimactic manor in which she is discovered, I'd say overall Hollyleaf is a welcome return. I was quite frustrated with her before she disappeared in Sunrise (in Po3) but she seems to have changed and I have to say I kinda like her again. She seems to have matured during her exile. She is as strategic and fair minded as she was, but there is a humbleness to her now. Before she had the prophecy hanging over her, now she knows she is excluded from it, and it seems to have given her pause. (I hope I won't regret writing this lol)... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This one ends on an obvious cliffhanger to the Dark Forest battle that looms over our heads till the 6th book comes out in like 6 months from now...no surprise there. I really enjoyed this addition to OotS and I seriously hope I can make it till book 6 comes out! Let the countdown begin :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9268501710542341797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13924021918241665581">Really good. <br/><br/>I’m happy Cinderheart finally knows who she is, and starting to accept it.   <span id="freeText13924021918241665581" style="display:none">Really good. <br /><br />I’m happy Cinderheart finally knows who she is, and starting to accept it. I really hope she and Lionblaze get together eventually, they deserve each other. <br /><br />I also hope Flametail will appear more. In the previous book I was slightly annoyed at how much we kept seeing him, and now we barely see him at all. I want to know how he is; it was saddening to see him in the Dark Forest briefly. <br /><br />I also don’t understand why Tigerheart stood on Dawnpelt’s side regarding the “murder” of Flametail. He had warned Dovewing and Ivypool, so why side with her now? I look forward to getting to know his motives. He seems like a good cat, so why is he in the Dark Forest? Will be very interesting to get to know. <br /><br />All in all, it was a good book with nice plot twists. I figured Hollyleaf would come back, and worried she’s the one who wanted revenge. What a relief that Sol was the traitor, not her! </span>

<div id="review_3065578381" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3065578381" />
    <a title="Historyprincess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12881308-historyprincess"><img alt="Historyprincess" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3065578381?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Historyprincess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Historyprincess" href="/user/show/12881308-historyprincess">Historyprincess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/32328620-the-forgotten-warrior">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12881308-historyprincess?shelf=warriors">warriors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3065578381&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3065578381" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9335388786542547004">Premise: "The end of the stars draws near. Three must become four to challenge the darkness that lasts forever…" The words of this prophecy become clearer to Jayfeather, Lionblaze, and Dovewing every day as they wait to do battle with the Dark Forest. Meanwhile, Ivypool is determined to continue spying on the enemy for the Three, despite the ever increasing danger. And in the midst of the growing turmoil, two cats once thought to be gone for good return to the Clans yet again. But which has come</span>
  <span id="freeText9335388786542547004" style="display:none">Premise: "The end of the stars draws near. Three must become four to challenge the darkness that lasts forever…" The words of this prophecy become clearer to Jayfeather, Lionblaze, and Dovewing every day as they wait to do battle with the Dark Forest. Meanwhile, Ivypool is determined to continue spying on the enemy for the Three, despite the ever increasing danger. And in the midst of the growing turmoil, two cats once thought to be gone for good return to the Clans yet again. But which has come in peace, and which has come to wreak havoc?<br /><br />Story/Writing: Geez, I have to give these authors mad praise once again! I've always been impressed at how they can come up with story ideas that at first on paper (no pun intended) would feel short and cheap. And in the hands of lesser writers, they probably would be. But the Erin Hunter team masterfully paints vivid pictures with their words and executes these ideas with ease! I will admit, my memory of this book is slightly choppier than usual, but that's mainly because the three days in which I read it were pretty busy, and I couldn't get through it as fast as I wanted to. That said, this book is a true page-turner in every sense of the word! It's funny because given that these arcs have six books in them each, I always come to the fifth ones not completely certain about what my expectations are. But that in no way diminishes the impact they have! They set the stage for the sixth book while standing out on its own, which is fantastic! The authors once again weave their ideas together in a way that feels totally organic and natural. Not only that, they also once again prove they have the talent of coming up with ideas most of us probably wouldn't think of, such as Dawnpelt deluding herself into believing Jayfeather let her brother die on purpose. Even better though, they also prove once more that they know how to put characters in certain places while letting those characters go through an arc at the same time. In previous titles it was about Ivypool being lured into joining the Dark Forest and then deciding to spy on them for the Three. Here, Cinderheart tries to come to terms about who she is while also getting used to the medicine skills she had in her past life, which could prove highly important in the battle with the Dark Forest. Just masterful, masterful storytelling that had me reading, even when I was tired from what was happening in the three days I read it!<br /><br />Characters: If there's something the Erin Hunter team has also mastered, it's character development. Like I said, they not only put characters in specific places by having them go through their own arc; they also know how to use returning characters in a way that doesn't feel like cheap fan service, but rather integral to the plot. If anything, this book features the return of one of my favorite heroes and one of my favorite villains in this series!<br /><br />Dovewing – Let me start off with Dovewing by saying that I thought it was a brilliant idea to have Dovewing lose her sense for awhile and to give her a bit of post-traumatic stress, both caused by her journey into the mountains in the previous book. It makes her all the more sympathetic and all the more believable. She has nightmares where she relives the terrible memory of seeing Swoop taken by an eagle; and whenever she tries to reach out with her senses (at least in the first half of the book), she finds that they're blocked. Fortunately she regains her senses just in time to hear Sorreltail go into labor, as well as the hostile WindClan warriors when they come to attack ThunderClan at the end. And luckily, even though she has a bit of post-traumatic stress and doesn't immediately shake it off. She's not an overly dramatic stick-in-the-mud either. She's still involved with in Clan life and she's retained her bold and sometimes snarky attitude. One of my favorite quotes from her now is this: "Dawnpelt needs to grow up!" Speaking of which, I will admit I am a little disappointed that she and Tigerheart aren't together anymore, but I'll also admit that I saw the wisdom in it not continuing. Dovewing now firmly knows where her loyalties lie, and she lets Tigerheart know it by telling him off when he tries to warn her about Dawnpelt. Granted, she probably could've taken it a bit more seriously, and that likely was what ultimately turned Tigerheart off to her. But still, it was a great scene! I also thought her date with Bumblestripe was sweet and cute and romantic, and if they do get together, I hope they're happy! That said, she's seriously come such a long way from where she began. I can't wait to see her lead the final charge with Lionblaze and Jayfeather!<br /><br />Ivypool – Man, is Ivypool awesome in this book! I am kinda referring to one scene in particular, but I'll get to that in a bit. I seriously sympathized with her when she had to get the fox dirt and use it to guard Jayfeather's marigold plants from the rabbits, but that led the fox to the hollow nearby and it nearly ended up killing Molepaw and Cherrypaw. I also did kinda like the back-to-back scenes where she's hanging out with her and Dovewing's father, Birchfall, while Dovewing is hanging out with their mother, Whitewing. But I also seriously felt terrible for Ivypool when she found out that her own father was training in the Dark Forest, along with Blossomfall, and then she and her father just had to get into an argument with WindClan when they went to wash their paws in the stream. I also liked how she and Hollyleaf had this sort of aunt-niece relationship. All that said, just like her sister, Ivypool has also come a really long way, from the brat she had the tendency to be in this case. Now she's probably one of the fiercest warriors in the series, in every way! She is willing to do literally anything to get closer to the leaders of the Dark Forest and find out when the battle will be. Probably her best scene in the book is when she utterly slays Antpelt's spirit as a show of loyalty to the senior warriors in the Dark Forest. Yes, it is kinda sad that Antpelt died from his injuries he sustained there, but he also chose to stay there when he died. But still, she holds nothing back and claws the snot out of him! Not only that, she manages to scare Breezepelt and even Hawkfrost a little bit! Ivypool has proven herself to be probably one of the best warriors any of the Clans ever had. She's willing to go to extraordinary lengths most characters would probably back out of. That said of course, I'm holding my breath for when she finally betrays the Dark Forest when the battle comes.<br /><br />Lionblaze – Lionblaze was once again fantastic in this! I love how he has three simultaneous struggles going on. The first is obviously the continuing issue he has with Cinderheart, and how she doesn't believe she can't be his mate because of how important he is to the prophecy. But then they both find out how important she is as well, and it turns everything on its head. If only Lionblaze knew too though that he's the reincarnation (for lack of a better way to put it) of Lion's Roar. They'd at least have that shared struggle. In any event, I do hope they get together eventually 'cause they feel so right for each other. Anyway, I loved how he and Hollyleaf interacted in this as well! I love how he's determined at first to track down the intruder who fought off the fox, until he starts to think it could be her. And then when he actually does find her, he's not gonna let her run away again and becomes protective of her but not in a patronizing way. But of course, I absolutely loved how Lionblaze was the first one to find Sol, and how he was forced to deal with the fact that he'd helped Sol to escape from ThunderClan when the fox-heart was being held prisoner there. Really shows how your past actions can come back to haunt you. Once again, even if Lionblaze doesn't have the deepest character development, I loved what I got, and I can't wait to see him gather his strength (no pun intended) when he leads the fight against the Dark Forest!<br /><br />Jayfeather – Jayfeather also doesn't get the deepest character development in this. But as usual, it's great here! He knows he can't be the only medicine cat to serve ThunderClan when the final battle comes. He knows that won't be enough. So not only does he stand up to Yellowfang and tell her they need Leafpool's medicine skills, he also finally tells Cinderheart that she's the reincarnation (again, for lack of a better way to put it) of Cinderpelt! That was one of the best parts of the book, where he appears to Cinderheart in a dream and takes her through Cinderpelt's most important memories: Her time as Yellowfang's apprentice in the old forest, the way she helped cats from other Clans during the Great Journey, and of course, her utterly tragic death when she sacrificed herself to save Sorreltail from the badger – and right at the moment when Cinderheart was born. I love how sweetly and gently he talks to her, given he doesn't usually talk that way to many cats. But he knows her case is unique so it has to be dealt with as delicately as possible. He tells her that she's her own cat and that she should honor StarClan's gift of a second life to her, but also choose what she genuinely wants. Those were some of the best scenes in the book. I also loved his emotional reunion with his long-lost sister. And of course I felt awful for him when Dawnpelt accused him at the Gathering of murdering Flametail. But it was awesome when he defended himself and defied his fellow medicine cats when they told him to surrender his duties until further notice. In the end though, I just wonder how Jayfeather is gonna prepare for how bloody the final battle is going to be. Whatever the case ends up being, I hope he's ready.<br /><br />Hollyleaf – Now we come to the titular character and the cat on the cover (of the version I read)! One of my favorite characters in the series! Hollyleaf is BACK!!! Not only that, she's back in spectacular fashion! By which I mean she has to deal with so much so fast, but the way in which she does deal with it is awesome! She's been away from home and underground for at least eighteen months. She has to face her Clan and explain why she left and how it involved the death of Ashfur. And she has to face the other Clans at the first Gathering she's attended in moons, given how she revealed the shocking truth about her family at her last one. But she's just as tough and unwavering in her conviction as she ever was. More than that, contrary to how she thought her Clan would be better off without her, she ends up being just the cat they need at just the right time! It was so cool when she taught the cats of ThunderClan how to fight in the tunnels in case WindClan tries to invade. Even better, she leads the battle into the tunnels and works with Dovewing as she does, combining her knowledge of the tunnels and Dovewing's special senses. But easily her best moment is when she beats the snot out of Sol! Even if she does let him go, it fits with her character. Plus she proved how much of a better fighter she is! I hope she plays a part in the battle with the Dark Forest because she deserves to help out in my opinion!<br /><br />Various Other Characters – In addition to Hollyleaf, Sol comes back as well, and he's out for revenge! And fittingly enough, he attempts to get it in the most wickedly clever and sneakiest way possible, befriending both WindClan and ThunderClan cats and ultimately turning them against one another. I got so mad when he took credit for rescuing the apprentices from the fox, when it was Hollyleaf who did it! I admit I also kinda got frustrated about how ThunderClan seemed a bit too willing to let him back in. I certainly agree with them about how they shouldn't let the other Clans order them around, but WindClan also has a point. Sol has always proven himself to be bad business. And if he appears in the final battle, I won't be surprised if he's among the first to be struck down. I don't really blame Molepaw and Cherrypaw for liking him at first, given they weren't even born the last time he was here, and they believed at first that he saved them from the fox. That said, Molepaw and Cherrypaw were cute! I have to give Brambleclaw a massive amount of credit for standing up for Hollyleaf. Even if he did twist the story to make it sound like she killed Ashfur by accident, and even if he still hasn't made up with Squirrelflight, he knew where Hollyleaf was coming from and what she had been through, and he had compassion on her. And Cinderheart, man she was so good in this book! Whatever your beliefs about reincarnation, I found the way she dealt with the revelation about who she is to be realistic and poignant. I love how it was almost kind of traumatizing her, and that she doesn't know who she is or what she should be. That said, she proved she could be a big help for ThunderClan when she saves Mousewhisker and Cherrypaw from the poison of the hemlock. I also thought Bumblestripe's pursuit of Dovewing was sweet. Tigerheart, now that you've sided with your deluded sister, you're on my dislike list. Speaking of Dawnpelt, how did she get to be like this when she was cute and spunky as an apprentice? I know that was seasons ago now, and I get wanting to blame your brother's death on something other than the ice, but still! She has the gall to not only make an unfounded accusation of murder. She accuses one of the cats who played a major part in ridding her Clan of Sol. Even if things are not as stable as they used to be, that was low!<br /><br />Overall: This book does a stupendous job of raising the stakes for the survival of the Clans even higher. The tension between Clans, the medicine cats, and even StarClan is now at breaking point. And it looks like the Dark Forest is finally gonna make their move. On its own, this book was fantastic. But I absolutely cannot wait to see how it all builds to an explosive climax in "The Last Hope."</span>
  <a data-text-id="9335388786542547004" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7295610-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514783093p2/7295610.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/253839525?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/7295610-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer253839525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1979676002906154327">*This review was originally published on <a href='https://rachelpoli.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>RachelPoli.com</a><br/><br/>BOOK COVER<br/><br/>The book cover matches the rest of the series. It highlights a cat who’s important to the current book and series as a whole. I had guessed who the cat was on the front cover, even though that cat is no longer listed as one of the characters.<br/><br/>FIRST THOUGHTS<br/><br/>Since I knew who the “forgotten warrior” was, I was eager to get going on this fifth book. This cat hasn’t been seen for a while and I’ve missed her.<br/><br/>PLOT<br/><br/>A lot of the plot in this </span>
  <span id="freeText1979676002906154327" style="display:none">*This review was originally published on <a href="https://rachelpoli.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">RachelPoli.com</a><br /><br />BOOK COVER<br /><br />The book cover matches the rest of the series. It highlights a cat who’s important to the current book and series as a whole. I had guessed who the cat was on the front cover, even though that cat is no longer listed as one of the characters.<br /><br />FIRST THOUGHTS<br /><br />Since I knew who the “forgotten warrior” was, I was eager to get going on this fifth book. This cat hasn’t been seen for a while and I’ve missed her.<br /><br />PLOT<br /><br />A lot of the plot in this book is highlighting what’s already happened before and how the cats are dealing with it. Then an outsider shows up to help and that throws some characters for a loop. Overall, this plot was a lot of build up for the next book, the final in the Omen of the Stars installment.<br /><br />CHARACTERS<br /><br />A lot of this book focused on the forgotten warrior. Again, it was great to see her again after so long, even though it was easy to guess she’d be coming back. Overall, all the characters are great – Dovewing, Lionblaze, and Jayfeather – and it’s weird to know their story is coming to an end.<br /><br />WRITING STYLE<br /><br />As always, this is an easy read. The book flows well and while this wasn’t as tense as the previous books in the series, it was still a page-turner.<br /><br />OVERALL<br /><br />I enjoyed this book as much as I have the others and I’m looking forward to seeing the ending of Omen of the Stars in the next book.<br /><br />Favorite Quote:<br /><br />“Why do relationships have to be so complicated?” -Erin Hunter, Warriors: The Forgotten Warrior (Omen of the Stars 5)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1979676002906154327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

<span id="freeTextContainer16855369169581398304">I was really impressed by this next installation of the Warriors series.<br/><br/>Even though I was disappointed with the... plethora of repetitive phrases throughout the book, the storyline kinda made up for it. I was surprised how Hollyleaf changed when she came back; she seeemed really out of character. Oh, and congratulations, Bumblestripe, you just earned yourself a one-way ticket to my hate list! Why would you choose DOVEWING, a cat you might not have any hopes for, over your LITTERMATE? That really</span>
  <span id="freeText16855369169581398304" style="display:none">I was really impressed by this next installation of the Warriors series.<br /><br />Even though I was disappointed with the... plethora of repetitive phrases throughout the book, the storyline kinda made up for it. I was surprised how Hollyleaf changed when she came back; she seeemed really out of character. Oh, and congratulations, Bumblestripe, you just earned yourself a one-way ticket to my hate list! Why would you choose DOVEWING, a cat you might not have any hopes for, over your LITTERMATE? That really irked me. I also thought it was funny at how Whitewing had a mother-daughter moment with Dovewing while Jayfeather was being helped by Ivypool. Whitewing was being all "Oh, why don't you take a look at Bumblestripe?" and stuff. I hated how she kinda forced Dovewing to like Bumblestripe though. She's still clearly in denial with Tigerheart. She can't accept the fact that she still has those feelings for him.<br /><br />I loved the part where Cinderpelt came back as Cinderheart in her dreams, triggered by Jayfeather. The Erins couldn't have played out the scene any more clever than they already did! Flashbacks, just like the time in Eclipse when Jaypaw healed Cinderpaw's broken leg again.<br /><br />I didn't like the plot conversing and collaborating with Sol, nor WindClan. It just seemed like the Erins were poising WindClan as puppets. All those new warriors had no reason to fight ThunderClan. Sol made them look as mouse-brained as they could be, but he always does that to cats, so I guess it's not saying a lot.<br /><br />I was happy overall with this book, but it could have been better.</span>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39906995-the-lost-heir"><img alt="The Lost Heir (Wings of Fire Graphic Novel, #2)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1529759887l/39906995._SX98_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3VcB1KuaLHY3lSLil474vsND4HzTqam5HjiSf9LICRrjGnQJq8DZc0bB3wwAXdDDyOqVcXigIdq1A79JTalLAw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('w2/9il5w+XGP1hZPzl+iHUIAx+36eA4ZsLp1Q+KolHj9IohXXioMdP6C66FZjIpgSamy4FFxhnobgVh1fcnWYQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText10207219566263983366" style="display:none">Erin Hunter is the pseudonym of five people: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/132369.Kate_Cary" title="Kate Cary" rel="nofollow noopener">Kate Cary</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/220345.Cherith_Baldry" title="Cherith Baldry" rel="nofollow noopener">Cherith Baldry</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/374504.Tui_T__Sutherland" title="Tui T. Sutherland" rel="nofollow noopener">Tui T. Sutherland</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2742182.Gillian_Philip" title="Gillian Philip" rel="nofollow noopener">Gillian Philip</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/769868.Inbali_Iserles" title="Inbali Iserles" rel="nofollow noopener">Inbali Iserles</a>, as well as editor <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/645010.Victoria_Holmes" title="Victoria Holmes" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Holmes</a>. Together, they write the Warriors series as well as the Seekers and Survivors series. Erin Hunter is working on a new series now called Bravelands. <br /><br />Erin Hunter is inspired by a love of cats and a fascination with the ferocity of the natural world. As well as having a great respect for nature in all its forms, Erin enjoys creating rich mythical explanations for animal behavior, shaped by her interest in astronomy and standing stones.</span>
